    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText17811355175049448548" style="display:none"><i>I can't believe there's going to be a gay Jewish president.</i><br /><br />As my mother said this, she looked at my father, who was still staring at the screen. Duncan's boyfriend, Jimmy, is with him to celebrate. Love and kindness appear to have won the day.<br /><br />But all too quickly, things start to go wrong. The election is called into question... and Duncan and Jimmy's relationship is called into question, too. Suddenly Duncan has to decide what he's willing to risk for something he believes in... and how far he's willing to go to hold on to the people we hold dear.</span>

<div id="review_1627349489" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1627349489" />
    <a title="Vee S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3961054-vee-s"><img alt="Vee S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490670722p2/3961054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1627349489?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vee S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vee S" href="/user/show/3961054-vee-s">Vee S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961054-vee-s?shelf=queer-ya">queer-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627349489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3213519538693985828">Actual rating: 4.5 Stars <br/><br/>This book was so fantastic. How do I describe it? Basically, imagine if Bernie Sanders and Donald Trump won the nominations for their parties, only Bernie was gay and instead of being mostly focused on Wall Street &c he was more idealistic and about all of us coming together as "great community." Then imagine he's elected president, but the opponent refuses to concede the election and instead tries a mass voter disenfranchisement tactic to try and make himself the victor</span>
  <span id="freeText3213519538693985828" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5 Stars <br /><br />This book was so fantastic. How do I describe it? Basically, imagine if Bernie Sanders and Donald Trump won the nominations for their parties, only Bernie was gay and instead of being mostly focused on Wall Street &amp;c he was more idealistic and about all of us coming together as "great community." Then imagine he's elected president, but the opponent refuses to concede the election and instead tries a mass voter disenfranchisement tactic to try and make himself the victor. Also, imagine that someone very much like Donald Trump was already elected president last time around, and had actually done all the things that he said he's going to do, and America and the world is still reeling from the aftermath.<br /><br />Wide Awake is basically about that, and a young gay Jewish boy navigating his way through it, fighting against the voter disenfranchisement, and figuring out his relationship. I LOVED it. If I'd read this book a year ago I would've thought it was too unrealistic, that it would never happen. And there are certainly still parts that I hope to God won't happen, but given our current political state, they're now legitimate possibilities. So it was kinda great to see some of those possibilities explored.<br /><br />Wide Awake was also the best exploration of faith I've ever seen in a book. I loved the future of faith (and Christianity in particular) that David Levithan laid out. There's a "Jesus Revolution" that has taken place, which is basically a large amount of Christians saying heck no to the fear-mongering and judgment that other Christians preached. The depiction of faith was really, really lovely and made me hopeful for the future. <br /><br />There was one very odd bit having to do with a trans character, and a fair bit of misgendering. It wasn't exactly offensive or hurtful, at least not to me, it was simply... odd. There's also a bit where the main character talks about dressing up as Paul Revere dressing up as a "Mohican" for the Boston Tea Party, which... didn't seem like the greatest. <br /><br />Despite those two things, however, I thoroughly enjoyed this book. It was a quick, fun read, and I'd recommend it to anyone who enjoys politics or is looking to find a positive and affirming depiction of faith. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3213519538693985828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387458330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13741167474329585549">David Levithan's books make me so happy young people have access to his writing - perhaps making their personal journeys a bit less isolating and a lot more promising. Wide Awake in particular becomes a must-read YA novel in this insane election year. What a sense of hope Levithan gives all of us for a near-future full of possibility.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744356918" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12248943-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499990463p2/12248943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744356918?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/12248943-mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12248943-mike?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744356918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4214039356505597873">I want you to believe me when I say that David Levithan really is one of the best writers in YA. I won't pretend he's consistent, but when he's at his best (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262783.Every_Day__Every_Day___1_' title='Every Day (Every Day, #1) by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Every Day</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson' title='Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Will Grayson Will Grayson</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5982447.Love_Is_the_Higher_Law' title='Love Is the Higher Law by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Love is the Higher Law</a>), he creates complex characters, with strong voices, and unique premises that only could've come from him. He's also one of the best writers of LGBT fiction I can think of, except maybe Malinda Lo. He's one of the few authors who really explores the different people that identify a</span>
  <span id="freeText4214039356505597873" style="display:none">I want you to believe me when I say that David Levithan really is one of the best writers in YA. I won't pretend he's consistent, but when he's at his best (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262783.Every_Day__Every_Day___1_" title="Every Day (Every Day, #1) by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Day</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson Will Grayson</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5982447.Love_Is_the_Higher_Law" title="Love Is the Higher Law by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Love is the Higher Law</a>), he creates complex characters, with strong voices, and unique premises that only could've come from him. He's also one of the best writers of LGBT fiction I can think of, except maybe Malinda Lo. He's one of the few authors who really explores the different people that identify as gay, and what that identification means in the real world, all without writing stories that feel like vehicles for a positive message. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17237214.Two_Boys_Kissing" title="Two Boys Kissing by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Two Boys Kissing</a> is the best display of what it means to be a gay teenager I know of.<br /><br />I say all that because all that makes it all the more disappointing when he writes terrible books like this one. This fails at everything that Levithan would later succeed at in Two Boys Kissing - whereas the latter balances character development and a realistic political message, this is idealistic, unrealistic, with bland characters. It's a vehicle for Levithan's mainstream liberalism. The political message itself is far more flawed than the one that appears in Two Boys Kissing, and I plan on writing a piece commenting on that later. But here, I wanted to comment on this failing as a book, rather than Levithan's failing as a political commentator.<br /><br />The thing that stands out the most is how obvious it is that the characters and writing are Levithan's default. None of the secondary characters get any real development - they're all just nice, dedicated people. Duncan, our protagonist, is the only one that feels even remotely like a real person, and he's the same narrator that appears in a lot of Levithan's books. You could've called him Nick, Ely, Dash, the unnamed narrator of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9279177.The_Lover_s_Dictionary" title="The Lover's Dictionary by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lover's Dictionary</a>, or even A and I wouldn't have been able to tell the difference. Both in personality and voice, he's the same as all of those protagonists of Levithan's. This isn't the only time Levithan has focused on something other than character development - the focus of Love is the Higher Law was on New York in general, rather than the specific characters. But there, I never felt like Levithan had forgotten about developing his characters. They weren't the focus, but after reading the book, I still felt like I knew them. I still got a sense of their lives outside of the plot, I still felt like they were real. That's not the case here - for all I know, Duncan doesn't do anything other than go to political rallies. We know <i>nothing</i> about him except his views on politics. It's boring and frustrating.<br /><br />The plot itself is difficult to get into without talking about how I feel about Levithan's political views. But I will say this: the way Levithan set up his conflict was pretty frustrating. There really is no conflict outside of the broader politics, outside of the (completely predictable) question of whether or not Stein will be president or not. Duncan experiences no personal conflict. His character has no growth - Levithan doesn't even pretend. There is a minor conflict, among some of Duncan's friends, involving one of his friends cheating on another. But it's not at all engaging or necessary - it feels tacked on.<br /><br />There really is almost nothing at all to say about this book that doesn't have to do with Levithan's political opinion. This is a politically dominated book. Much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5470.1984" title="1984 by George Orwell" rel="nofollow noopener">1984</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17470674.Fahrenheit_451" title="Fahrenheit 451 by Ray Bradbury" rel="nofollow noopener">Fahrenheit 451</a>, it only exists for the purposes of being an essay. The best I can give it is that Levithan's prose is excellent is always. Other than that, this is Levithan's absolute worst book. The only other book of his that even comes close is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23230.Naomi_and_Ely_s_No_Kiss_List" title="Naomi and Ely's No Kiss List by Rachel Cohn" rel="nofollow noopener">Naomi and Ely's No-Kiss List</a>, and even then, the lack of quality was mostly Rachel Cohn's fault. Levithan has so many books that are far better than this - really, if you want to read David Levithan, I'd recommend any of his books over this one.<br /><br /><b>This review can also be found <a href="http://thelowercasegimmick.tumblr.com/post/147626886491/ya-review-7416-wide-awake-by-david-levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4214039356505597873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22129330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22129330?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22129330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16755224168054196617">Reviewed by Christian C. for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Decades from today, the results of the election are out, and for the first time in the history of the United States, a gay, Jewish president, Abraham Stein, has been elected. After the Greater Depression, the War to End All Wars, the Reign of Fear, and the Jesus Revolution, the moment has arrived. Seventeen-year-old Duncan, who has spent the last few months working with his boyfriend, Jimmy, as a volunteer at the campaign headquarters, can finally sta</span>
  <span id="freeText16755224168054196617" style="display:none">Reviewed by Christian C. for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Decades from today, the results of the election are out, and for the first time in the history of the United States, a gay, Jewish president, Abraham Stein, has been elected. After the Greater Depression, the War to End All Wars, the Reign of Fear, and the Jesus Revolution, the moment has arrived. Seventeen-year-old Duncan, who has spent the last few months working with his boyfriend, Jimmy, as a volunteer at the campaign headquarters, can finally stand up for the Pledge of Allegiance because at last the words "with liberty and justice for all" make sense. <br /><br />But soon everything will take a 180-degree turn. The governor of Kansas, a member of the opposition party, demands a recount. Stein is determined to fight back, and asks all the people who have elected him to go to Kansas and show their support. Everyone at the election headquarters decides to board their bus that night and join this pilgrimage to Kansas. <br /><br />Duncan, always insecure, always wondering about what Jimmy will think and what will happen to their relationship, knows that going to Kansas is the right thing to do. It's the once in a lifetime opportunity to help write history, and he decides to board the bus despite his parents' disapproval. <br /><br />However, the trip proves to be more challenging than he thought. Duncan and Jimmy's relationship seems strained. Their friend Keisha finds out that her girlfriend, Mira, was having an affair with another girl in the group. And when the group arrives in Topeka, Kansas, they have to endure the insults and vicious attacks of the Decents (the supporters of the opposition party). They camp out in the center of town, along with more than half a million other people, with not much food, only a few accommodations, and no quick resolution in sight. Will it be worth it? Will justice prevail? <br /><br />When I pick up a book by David Levithan, certain things are a given. First, I know it's going to be well written. From a little poem, to a presidential speech, to a sex scene, Levithan proves once again with WIDE AWAKE that he's a talented writer and has a great deal of imagination. This entertaining novel, full of interesting characters, is a combination of a fun parody of good versus evil, and a love story. </span>

<div id="review_124539827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124539827" />
    <a title="Sean Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2535186-sean-kennedy"><img alt="Sean Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442482458p2/2535186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124539827?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Kennedy" href="/user/show/2535186-sean-kennedy">Sean Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375834677" href="/book/show/2445580.Wide_Awake">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124539827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8768062699006059335">The two books I have read from David Levithan so far have required quite a bit of suspension of disbelief - in "Boy Meets Boy" it was a bit easier to get over the initial resistance to it, but "Wide Awake" suffers because of it. It's a shame, because it could have been a truly great and inspiring YA novel. Levithan's world-building always seems to push a bit too far - my first stumbling block was the notion that in the future we no longer shop for stuff, but just go to look at them and then dona</span>
  <span id="freeText8768062699006059335" style="display:none">The two books I have read from David Levithan so far have required quite a bit of suspension of disbelief - in "Boy Meets Boy" it was a bit easier to get over the initial resistance to it, but "Wide Awake" suffers because of it. It's a shame, because it could have been a truly great and inspiring YA novel. Levithan's world-building always seems to push a bit too far - my first stumbling block was the notion that in the future we no longer shop for stuff, but just go to look at them and then donate the money we would have spent to charity. Huh? Sorry, hopefully humans will evolve more socio-politically as time passes, but we are still materialistic creatures at heart. The other stumbling block is that, in a book full of pop-culture references, the song "A Boy Named Sue" is used as a plot point - as in, we meet a character named Sue who is living the life of the character from that song. I kept waiting for this point to be referenced, or for it to be explained more as the book progressed, but it wasn't. It just stuck out like a sore thumb and I didn't see why it was used at all.<br /><br />I feel like I am focusing on the negative aspects too much - there are some really good parts to this book as well and I still recommend it as a read. Your suspension of disbelief may be easier to dial down than mine was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8768062699006059335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia" href="/user/show/1331593-lydia">Lydia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63089175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12329959745312094739">This is a most interesting YA read.<br/><br/>The U.S. has an elected a gay, Jewish president -- or so it seems until Kansas decides maybe the count is off. The group of 16-yr old teens who worked so hard on the campaign are devastated, just as the "Decents" who opposed the candidate are. The tag line of the book is "What are you willing to do for what you believe in?"<br/><br/>Levithan is an excellent writer and may have missed his calling when he decided not to become a political speechwriter (the speeches by the </span>
  <span id="freeText12329959745312094739" style="display:none">This is a most interesting YA read.<br /><br />The U.S. has an elected a gay, Jewish president -- or so it seems until Kansas decides maybe the count is off. The group of 16-yr old teens who worked so hard on the campaign are devastated, just as the "Decents" who opposed the candidate are. The tag line of the book is "What are you willing to do for what you believe in?"<br /><br />Levithan is an excellent writer and may have missed his calling when he decided not to become a political speechwriter (the speeches by the elected officials in the books are outstanding). Plus, he has a sense of humor (as when you meet the boy named Sue who looks for his father, who is now Loretta). The questions posed in this book are valuable and relevant to teen life, no matter what the beliefs. Perhaps one of the most interesting perspectives is that the candidate is elected thanks to the "Jesus Freaks" -- an absolutely fascinating perspective on how values coincide.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12329959745312094739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3461910065" />
    <a title="Ulysses Dietz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5510714-ulysses-dietz"><img alt="Ulysses Dietz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365337579p2/5510714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3461910065?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ulysses Dietz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ulysses Dietz" href="/user/show/5510714-ulysses-dietz">Ulysses Dietz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6639103-wide-awake">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3461910065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11561803172931490808">Wide Awake<br/>By David Levithan<br/>Alfred A. Knopf, 2006 (Kindle edition 2016)<br/>Five stars<br/><br/>“What are you willing to do for something you believe in?”<br/><br/>Wide awake is a YA story, about a sixteen-year-old gay Jewish boy and his mixed-race boyfriend, who make a pilgrimage to Kansas to help prevent that state’s governor from overturning the legitimate election of the first gay, Jewish president. <br/><br/>First published in 2006, Levithan offers an afterword to this 2016 edition written in the summer of that year. What he,</span>
  <span id="freeText11561803172931490808" style="display:none">Wide Awake<br />By David Levithan<br />Alfred A. Knopf, 2006 (Kindle edition 2016)<br />Five stars<br /><br />“What are you willing to do for something you believe in?”<br /><br />Wide awake is a YA story, about a sixteen-year-old gay Jewish boy and his mixed-race boyfriend, who make a pilgrimage to Kansas to help prevent that state’s governor from overturning the legitimate election of the first gay, Jewish president. <br /><br />First published in 2006, Levithan offers an afterword to this 2016 edition written in the summer of that year. What he, of course, couldn’t know was that four years later, the full power of his story’s worst-case scenario is still upon us, made worse and more surreal by the global pandemic that has engulfed us all due to the utter failure of our national leadership.<br /><br />Duncan and Jimmy and their friends live in a weirdly plausible not-quite-dystopian USA that has been dragged through the Greater Depression and the War to End All Wars and something referred to simply as the Reign of Fear. Otherwise, they are pretty typical teenagers, struggling with notions of independence and romance as teenagers always have. Levithan uses all sorts of clever details to remind us that this is not the world we know (or knew in 2006) but, rather, a world that we might come to know someday. These are good kids, and as is typical of so many YA novels, their parents barely register on the page. I was relieved and comforted that, while the parents never matter much in the action, they are there, and they are not entirely powerless or pointless. <br /><br />Duncan and Jimmy and their friends—including the older folks who make the pilgrimage to Kansas possible—are great people, people I’d be proud to know. The most fascinating detail of this future world is an apparent alliance of liberally minded evangelical Christians and LGBTQ youth. This vision of a world where liberal Christians (or, as I like to think of them, actual Christians) embrace ideas of life, liberty and the pursuit of happiness for everyone brought tears to my eyes, and more than once.<br /><br />I’ve had this book on my Kindle for a while, and I’m glad I chose this moment to read it. Levithan is probably more appalled than I am at the state of the nation right now, but his faith in people as expressed in this book gave me hope.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11561803172931490808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236046384" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1118065-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218130576p2/1118065.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375834677" href="/book/show/2445580.Wide_Awake">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not too sure</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1118065-nicole?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1118065-nicole?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1118065-nicole?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236046384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6930463634286109604">Can it be historical fiction if it's set in a fictional future? Because this book is all about making history...in the future. When a gay Jewish man becomes president. You know, when that happens. Someday. Maybe. Possibly...<br/><br/>This was not my favorite Levithan and I've been trying to work out why this book didn't sear into my soul like his other books. (Alright, maybe not my soul, but definitely into my beneath the surface emotions. Definitely there.)<br/><br/>I think it's because this book felt like a proje</span>
  <span id="freeText6930463634286109604" style="display:none">Can it be historical fiction if it's set in a fictional future? Because this book is all about making history...in the future. When a gay Jewish man becomes president. You know, when that happens. Someday. Maybe. Possibly...<br /><br />This was not my favorite Levithan and I've been trying to work out why this book didn't sear into my soul like his other books. (Alright, maybe not my soul, but definitely into my beneath the surface emotions. Definitely there.)<br /><br />I think it's because this book felt like a project. It felt forced. It felt like every word was constructed not to woo the reader, but to sway the reader. It felt like a political campaign: Read my book! Think like me! Make the future match my ideal! I wasn't able to get lost in the characters because the characters were simply props used to make Levithan's point. Not unlike _Unbearable Lightness of Being_ except that Kundera was brilliant and kept you caring for his stick characters while Levithan's stick characters leave a dry, dissatisfying taste in your mouth. I felt like I was being persuaded and it was not a pleasent feeling.<br /><br />The setting of this futuristic novel, however, felt very possible to me. Of course there will be another world war and of course gas prices will be $30/gal and of course there will be non-malls. Intriguing, that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6930463634286109604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1421654173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421654173" />
    <a title="Sleepless Dreamer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7614560-sleepless-dreamer"><img alt="Sleepless Dreamer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431177042p2/7614560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421654173?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sleepless Dreamer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sleepless Dreamer" href="/user/show/7614560-sleepless-dreamer">Sleepless Dreamer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421654173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13831668933115923555">David Levithan is one of my favorite ya contemporary authors. That said, this book was a miss. David Levithan's books are truly amazing (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9279177.The_Lover_s_Dictionary' title='The Lover's Dictionary by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lover's Dictionary</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262783.Every_Day__Every_Day___1_' title='Every Day (Every Day, #1) by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Every Day</a>,and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23232.The_Realm_of_Possibility' title='The Realm of Possibility by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Realm of Possibility</a> are all wonderful) but this book just fell lame for me. <br/><br/>I thought I'd love this. As a Jewish gay (if we use the umbrella term gay for everyone who isn't straight), I thought this would resound with me. Yet I didn't feel it. In David Levithan's books, I normally feel like I get a real sense of who th</span>
  <span id="freeText13831668933115923555" style="display:none">David Levithan is one of my favorite ya contemporary authors. That said, this book was a miss. David Levithan's books are truly amazing (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9279177.The_Lover_s_Dictionary" title="The Lover's Dictionary by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lover's Dictionary</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262783.Every_Day__Every_Day___1_" title="Every Day (Every Day, #1) by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Day</a>,and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23232.The_Realm_of_Possibility" title="The Realm of Possibility by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Realm of Possibility</a> are all wonderful) but this book just fell lame for me. <br /><br />I thought I'd love this. As a Jewish gay (if we use the umbrella term gay for everyone who isn't straight), I thought this would resound with me. Yet I didn't feel it. In David Levithan's books, I normally feel like I get a real sense of who the person is. Here, I just didn't. I didn't feel connected to the characters. Any of them, apart from maybe Sue. <br /><br />Moreover, I'd hoped to feel that change, to get that feeling of becoming a better nation, a better community. I remember how overjoyed I felt when the USA legalized marriage. I felt like we won, like there was a victory for my side. I'd hoped to feel the same while reading this. Instead, I just didn't. I didn't believe this world. Something just struck me as unbelievable. <br /><br /> I disliked how Levithan attempts to showcase both Judaism and Christianity. It felt like he was trying to portray both of them, to show them both. Being me, I felt that Judaism was used to push the author's own political stance (which I generally agree with). Don't use our history for your agenda. I also felt Judaism played an infinitely small part next to Christianity. It was all about being like Jesus. I did like the portrayal of Jesus though. <br /><br />One thing I will say, David Levithan writes non straight characters and I love it. We need more. Of course, there's more to the community than gay and lesbian. Where are my asexual, aromantic, pansexul, demisxual, bisxual, intersex and nonbinary characters at? Still, it's not his burden to write those characters and I'm just being pedantic so I'll shut up.<br /><br />All in all, it's not a bad book. It's just not his best book, not by a long shot. <br /><br />Also heck yeah, I'm eight books ahead in my challenge. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13831668933115923555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/2004532-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375891465" href="/book/show/7312370-wide-awake">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jared Criswell</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2004532-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2004532-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2119836206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13039275414843092661">David Levithan's future is the first one I've read I would actually want to live in! I treasure his optimism. An America that again merits the name of democracy--equal justice for all--would be worth fighting to achieve. Instead we have our political reality in all its intolerance and ugliness. A book about the President stealing the election via shenanigans with the electoral college, while losing the popular vote, is all too familiar. <br/><br/>But politics is just one aspect of the story--there's also </span>
  <span id="freeText13039275414843092661" style="display:none">David Levithan's future is the first one I've read I would actually want to live in! I treasure his optimism. An America that again merits the name of democracy--equal justice for all--would be worth fighting to achieve. Instead we have our political reality in all its intolerance and ugliness. A book about the President stealing the election via shenanigans with the electoral college, while losing the popular vote, is all too familiar. <br /><br />But politics is just one aspect of the story--there's also teenage romance! His characters are people I care about, some more deeply than others, but their journey together is quite remarkable. His boys in love are adorable, as is the older couple who dust off their protest signs. And Gus! And Sue! I loved Sue (can't say more without a spoiler). <br /><br />The ebook edition I read includes an author's note on the 10th anniversary of the book's release in July 2016. In the run-up to the 2016 election, the author's fears for the future are unfortunately well-founded. This edition also includes his Margaret A. Edwards Award acceptance speech, in which he acknowledges the lineage of YA authors who have likewise been honored not for a single book but for a body of work that consistently delivers a clear and coherent message of hope for the future. He also scorches the committee that so honored Orson Scott Card, while it willfully set aside the man's homophobia, bigotry and dogmatism. Yes, thank you, Mr. Levithan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13039275414843092661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203540663" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203540663" />
    <a title="Cara M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5735243-cara-m"><img alt="Cara M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348195467p2/5735243.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203540663?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara M" href="/user/show/5735243-cara-m">Cara M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203540663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4285223219066011376">David Levithan was recommended to me as an author who could write about homosexuality front and center and give it a happy ending. But this book was not really what I was looking for. It was an interesting journal of a political movement, but honestly, it was really a one note samba. It definitely wanted to give a positive message, but the nuance it had in the beginning was swept away as Duncan joined the protest.<br/>In the end, the only thing i found convincing about the book was the relationships.</span>
  <span id="freeText4285223219066011376" style="display:none">David Levithan was recommended to me as an author who could write about homosexuality front and center and give it a happy ending. But this book was not really what I was looking for. It was an interesting journal of a political movement, but honestly, it was really a one note samba. It definitely wanted to give a positive message, but the nuance it had in the beginning was swept away as Duncan joined the protest.<br />In the end, the only thing i found convincing about the book was the relationships. Duncan was a mushy egg. Jimmy was awful, insensitive, careless and selfish, even as he pretended to be entirely of noble motive. None of the girls actually got any characterization. There were just the lesbians and the Jesus Freaks, nothing more complex. The truth is, even though it dealt with 'issues' like homosexuality and prejudice, this was really an MG novel, not YA. It was interesting, but very, very simple. At first i was worried something bad would happen, and then, about halfway though, i was angry that it hadn't.<br />In the end, this was a fantasy about how the Al Gore election should have gone, but it didn't work out that way, and as even the Obama election isn't working out all that well, it just becomes more and more of a tragedy, a tragedy where you can't even trust in your own feelings, because love will betray you too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4285223219066011376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37160362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37160362" />
    <a title="Chicklit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120407-chicklit"><img alt="Chicklit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204480767p2/120407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37160362?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chicklit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chicklit" href="/user/show/120407-chicklit">Chicklit</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120407-chicklit?shelf=ya_lit">ya_lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/120407-chicklit?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37160362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer598349997961219436">There are three things about David Levithan's books that I adore: the tenderness with which the protagonist views the world, the writing that has so much energy it seems to pop off the page, and finally, the creation of a world that is so idealistic and believable that I want to pack my bags and move to it. It's the last one that I had a problem with in this book.<br/><br/><i>Wide Awake</i> is set sometime in the distant future where teens hang out at non-shopping malls and give their money to charity rather tha</span>
  <span id="freeText598349997961219436" style="display:none">There are three things about David Levithan's books that I adore: the tenderness with which the protagonist views the world, the writing that has so much energy it seems to pop off the page, and finally, the creation of a world that is so idealistic and believable that I want to pack my bags and move to it. It's the last one that I had a problem with in this book.<br /><br /><i>Wide Awake</i> is set sometime in the distant future where teens hang out at non-shopping malls and give their money to charity rather than spend it on CDs and clothing, being gay is no big thing, America has just elected its first gay, Jewish president. To be clear, I'd back my bags and move to this America in a heartbeat, if I believed it could exist. <br /><br />So part of my ambivalence to the story is my cynicism, but the other part is that the messages seem so heavy handed. Early in the book the social commentary and political statements overtook the characters and the story.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="598349997961219436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309840219?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309840219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1200022785015361929">A huge disappointment after Boy Meets Boy. This novel was way too preachy, I felt like Levithan hammered me over the head with his message at every point. Where Boy Meets Boy was beautiful, funny and sad, Wide Awake was just... boring. I felt no sort of relationship with the characters at all, there was never any doubt as to how it all would turn out, and the beautiful phrases that had made Boy Meets Boy such a joy to read was sorely lacking from this novel. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1103717188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_497739213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497739213" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3835702-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357322828p2/3835702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/497739213?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/3835702-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375834677" href="/book/show/2445580.Wide_Awake">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=udate">udate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497739213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12773503613565196194">Reading the synopsis of Wide Awake, I found it difficult to see how David Levithan could pack religion, politics and sexuality into a book that's just over 200 pages long and make it meaningful. It's a minefield of hot topics that could have been awkward, preachy or uncomfortably controversial.<br/><br/>But in true David Levithan style, he takes a story and completely ensnared me in the life of Duncan, his boyfriend Jimmy, his friends and a cast of characters caught up in the election of the first gay Jew</span>
  <span id="freeText12773503613565196194" style="display:none">Reading the synopsis of Wide Awake, I found it difficult to see how David Levithan could pack religion, politics and sexuality into a book that's just over 200 pages long and make it meaningful. It's a minefield of hot topics that could have been awkward, preachy or uncomfortably controversial.<br /><br />But in true David Levithan style, he takes a story and completely ensnared me in the life of Duncan, his boyfriend Jimmy, his friends and a cast of characters caught up in the election of the first gay Jewish president of the United States. Jimmy's world is similar to ours now, but global recession, war and terrorism have greatly changed the political and religious outlook of America and the rest of the world. <br /><br />Duncan is a sweet, rather naive boy who seems to believe that what is right will always win - and it's an endearing quality rather than a frustrating one, as the story of his journey in realising that the world can be a frightening and pretty unfriendly place when you are different. In his home town, with his family and friends, his religion, sexuality and political beliefs are fairly widely accepted, with a few exceptions among his peers and with one particularly nasty teacher.<br /><br />Jimmy is rather more dark and negative, but with Duncan as his partner they balance each other perfectly. There's a fantastic supporting cast of teen and adult characters that make for a memorable group of people who are simply standing up for what they believe in, without any doubts that their cause will fail.<br /><br />I love that David Levithan took a world that could have been dark and disturbing and made it into an exciting, interesting take on what change could really mean. Although there are still divisions between religious and political beliefs, there are also groups that have changed how they interact with each other to make a more varied, joined country. As an imagining, this world felt like a real possibility.<br /><br />I enjoyed Wide Awake far more than I thought I would given the synopsis, and I loved returning to David Levithan's imagination.<br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a href="http://www.theaussiezombie.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Aussie Zombie</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12773503613565196194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442510715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6839412582881445701"><s>Making this quick and short because it's been four days since I've read the book and a crossover between Rise of the Guardians and How to Tame your Dragons is waiting for me in another tab. I will say sorry in advance for such a halfhearted review</s><br/><br/>A Gay Jewish President? Well, I'm not as surprised after reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23228.Boy_Meets_Boy' title='Boy Meets Boy by David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Boy Meets Boy</a>. It's idealistic. Fantastical. Impractical. And Fanciful. But nevertheless, pretty good once you wrap your mind around the fact that it's fiction and decide to <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395602i/761986._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Gotta admit i</span>
  <span id="freeText6839412582881445701" style="display:none"><s>Making this quick and short because it's been four days since I've read the book and a crossover between Rise of the Guardians and How to Tame your Dragons is waiting for me in another tab. I will say sorry in advance for such a halfhearted review</s><br><br>A Gay Jewish President? Well, I'm not as surprised after reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23228.Boy_Meets_Boy" title="Boy Meets Boy by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Boy Meets Boy</a>. It's idealistic. Fantastical. Impractical. And Fanciful. But nevertheless, pretty good once you wrap your mind around the fact that it's fiction and decide to <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395602i/761986._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Gotta admit it took me a few pages to do so. I'm a realist and half the time also a pessimist. When I dislike something, there's a tendency I'd lash out against it, especially when said it is defenseless and just begging to be bashed. <br><br><b>Wide Awake</b> <i>might</i> have ended up with the sharp end of my knife but seeing as I've read something of Levithan's before, I've steeled myself up against possible barfing unreasonable rainbows. And to my surprise, it worked. I actually <i>liked</i> it to some extent because I knew what to expect. My expectations weren't too high nor were they too low. Get pass the slightly one dimensional characters and you'll get a very inspiring, open YA book. [Levithan's writing style does help in a great way (because I know for sure that if the style was of lower quality,I wouldn't have given this book a second thought, so, yehey for Levithan!)] <br><br>To conclude,<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because Gaia, I can hear the fanfic calling for me and really, I'm sorry but I have no self control! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> it's a book that made me want to MOVE for something I'd want to live for (after making me feel like a sack of potato, that is). <br><br><b>Recommended</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6839412582881445701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_407636161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407636161" />
    <a title="Mersini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6599279-mersini"><img alt="Mersini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347354093p2/6599279.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407636161?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mersini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mersini" href="/user/show/6599279-mersini">Mersini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375834677" href="/book/show/2445580.Wide_Awake">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6599279-mersini?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6599279-mersini?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6599279-mersini?shelf=used-to-own">used-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407636161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer609438357086375173">Honestly, not really impressed by this novel. As far as the Goodreads rating system goes, I should probably give it 2 stars, but I feel that doesn't really show how I feel about it, so 3 it is. Basically, this is a novel about history in the making - in the future. It's a little confusing, I suppose, but not so much when you read it. <br/><br/>The problem I have here is that Levithan's characters are so one dimensional they're practically stereotypes. Not quite, but almost. In a young adult novel, is it t</span>
  <span id="freeText609438357086375173" style="display:none">Honestly, not really impressed by this novel. As far as the Goodreads rating system goes, I should probably give it 2 stars, but I feel that doesn't really show how I feel about it, so 3 it is. Basically, this is a novel about history in the making - in the future. It's a little confusing, I suppose, but not so much when you read it. <br /><br />The problem I have here is that Levithan's characters are so one dimensional they're practically stereotypes. Not quite, but almost. In a young adult novel, is it too much to ask for for characters to sound like people? It's not a children's fairytale, after all, you can't get away with transparency in your characters. Compound this with the fact that the plot is also very straight forward, without a real climax that involves confrontation, that the characters don't face a real struggle, either emotional or physical, or, when they do, Levithan writes it as he writes his characters: one dimensional, almost as if he's skimming over it. Maybe that's the real problem I have with Levithan's novels, the wasted potential. This is the fourth of his novels I've read, and while Love is the Higher Law and Every Me, Every You were quite good, particularly the former in its emotional depth, this novel and Boy Meets Boy were very shallow. Yes, it's nice to have an LGBT novel that's light, with a happy ending, but there is such a thing as too light. If this novel were longer, delving in and exploring the various characters' emotional complexities and their relationships with one another, still keeping the exact same plot, it would have been utterly fantastic. But it didn't, so it disappoints. <br /><br />Still, for what it's worth, it's nice when you don't want to read something too heavy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="609438357086375173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6702302905968539240">For such a short read this book contains an alarming amount of brilliant ideas and predictions for our countries not too distance future. I would love to see the day were a Jewish gay president is elected into office. It's amazing that this book was originally published in 2006 and how it holds even more true today.   <span id="freeText6702302905968539240" style="display:none">For such a short read this book contains an alarming amount of brilliant ideas and predictions for our countries not too distance future. I would love to see the day were a Jewish gay president is elected into office. It's amazing that this book was originally published in 2006 and how it holds even more true today. Levithan's insight is incredibly although I feel that his optimism is a bit too strong. As much as I would love nothing more than to see our society progress to a "greater community" i still feel that there are way too many "Decents" fighting back. I would like to see Levithan's projection on gun control. One of my favorite ideas from the novel was the "non mall". Instead of window shopping with friends and eventually becoming a hoarder you would have the experience and spend the money but it would go towards a charity and you would leave empty handed. Think of all the money that gets spend on things we don't need and often times really want. I know that I have been guilty of this more than I would like to admit. We are a society of over consumption on so many levels and it breaks my heart to think about it. If we had less and gave more the chance of us reaching a more peaceful, happy, and productive society/community would be all the greater. I don't think we will get close to Levithan's ideals in my lifetime but I'd like to believe if I have children they have a chance to live in a more loved community. </span>

<div id="review_5695254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5695254" />
    <a title="Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/232263-jean"><img alt="Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185649609p2/232263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5695254?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean" href="/user/show/232263-jean">Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5695254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1521063251314195739">What happens to good book ideas when they go bad? If you are a respected author/editor like David Levithan, they get published anyway. I really wanted to like this book. I'm from Kansas and I'm reasonably liberal, so a book based on the premise that in the future a Gay man or a Jewish man (or a combo) can run on a ticket with a Black/Latina/Lesbian for the President of the US is something that I thought I would enjoy. Unfortunately, Levithan got carried away with himself and his cleverness. Ther</span>
  <span id="freeText1521063251314195739" style="display:none">What happens to good book ideas when they go bad? If you are a respected author/editor like David Levithan, they get published anyway. I really wanted to like this book. I'm from Kansas and I'm reasonably liberal, so a book based on the premise that in the future a Gay man or a Jewish man (or a combo) can run on a ticket with a Black/Latina/Lesbian for the President of the US is something that I thought I would enjoy. Unfortunately, Levithan got carried away with himself and his cleverness. There is teen-age angst, political statements, social commentary, religious exploration, relationship shifting, and a road trip all rolled in to one. Throw in way too many references to old songs and the book just about topples over. I almost threw the book across the room when the boy named Sue showed up. Come on, David, get a little more original than that! (Although probably none of the intended audience would get the tip of the hat to Johnny Cash in that one.) It is obvious that Levithan has something to say about the war in Iraq, the state of politics and economics, and the possibility that one of these days gays and lesbians will be accepted for themselves, not judged on who they love. I hope the next try at saying something about one of these doesn't implode like this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1521063251314195739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17300952277159074910">I love David Levithan's futuristic fantasy: some decades from now, a gay Jewish man is elected as president. Predictably, the political forces against him try to shenanigate and gerrymander to steal the election back. Can a Gandhi-inspired crowd hold back such political evil? Of course Levithan is speaking to present-day America, and to all people everywhere hoping for a more equal, inclusive and fair life for everyone. Should we be realistic, idealistic or fatalistic? Through it all, different </span>
  <span id="freeText17300952277159074910" style="display:none">I love David Levithan's futuristic fantasy: some decades from now, a gay Jewish man is elected as president. Predictably, the political forces against him try to shenanigate and gerrymander to steal the election back. Can a Gandhi-inspired crowd hold back such political evil? Of course Levithan is speaking to present-day America, and to all people everywhere hoping for a more equal, inclusive and fair life for everyone. Should we be realistic, idealistic or fatalistic? Through it all, different relationships and their complexities are considered. However, the narrative never becomes heavy or overwrought. This novel becomes a totally likeable story with its heart on its sleeve.<br /><br />David Levithan se roman met 'n sestienjarige eerstepersoonsverteller speel dekades in die toekoms af en handel oor 'n Amerikaanse presidentsverkiesing waarin teenstanders van verandering die uitkoms probeer ontken en bekonkel. Natuurlik spreek die verhaal tot hedendaagse lesers: die scenario is geensins onbekend nie. Tussendeur skep besonderhede van verskeie liefdesverhoudings 'n menslike atmosfeer: Levithan kyk diep in die siel van sy karakters in. Die roman dra sy hart deeglik op die mou, en dit is waarom dit in dié leser se hart inkruip.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer667564549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1271625476297233251">I'm a fan of David Levithan. His characters feel like old friends from the very beginning of his books. Duncan and Jimmy are no exception - their relationship isn't perfect, but it is beautiful and lyrical and touching. <br/><br/>The story, centering around a contested election involving the first gay Jewish president, definitely made me think and wonder about the future. Could this be possible someday? If this could be possible, what else about our world could change? I enjoy finding books that ask big q</span>
  <span id="freeText1271625476297233251" style="display:none">I'm a fan of David Levithan. His characters feel like old friends from the very beginning of his books. Duncan and Jimmy are no exception - their relationship isn't perfect, but it is beautiful and lyrical and touching. <br /><br />The story, centering around a contested election involving the first gay Jewish president, definitely made me think and wonder about the future. Could this be possible someday? If this could be possible, what else about our world could change? I enjoy finding books that ask big questions and allow me to consider the answers for myself.<br /><br />Levithan definitely leans on some stereotypes in order to get his point across (read "Decents" as "Republicans") but most of his characters are refreshingly quirky and intriguing. I particularly loved Elwood, the adorable almost-thirteen-year-old who wants to convert to Judaism. As a gay Jew himself, he writes about Judaism with clear love and affection (in most, if not all of his books, not just this one). <br /><br /><u>Wide Awake</u> is a quick read, but will leave you mulling it over long after you finish it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1271625476297233251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('L+tERi1guiG/gYj7x3gznaw+CZOolhtZ9cTsrVAIQj4UQzdjr0F1YsccW9SV6IhYVsWGB/a/6kY+cpqROzho3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }
